  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_41887e0d-9119-43ee-a205-53b88cc97c7d'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initializeSiwa();

  <span id="freeText13589854475244228839" style="display:none">A thrilling story of friendship, survival, and the need to belong.<br /><br />For two moons Torak has hidden a terrible secret—and now it is revealed. He bears the mark of the Soul-Eater, and must pay the price. Cast out from the clans, he is alone and on the run: cut off from his best friend, Renn, and his beloved pack-brother, Wolf.<br /><br />He flees to the haunted reed-beds of Lake Axehead, where he is hunted by the Otter Clan, taunted by the Hidden People, and, as soul-sickness claims him, he falls prey to an even greater menace. Tormented by secrets and broken trust, he uncovers a deception that will turn his world upside down.</span>

Starting with this book will be difficult, as you will not know who the Soul Eaters were and why they are so feared. <div id="review_532784073" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/532784073" />
    <a title="Maythavee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12969590-maythavee"><img alt="Maythavee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513161414p2/12969590.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/532784073?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maythavee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maythavee" href="/user/show/12969590-maythavee">Maythavee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12969590-maythavee?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer532784073" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18270085842618374559">This series just keeps getting better and better! Outcast was a non-stop thrilling adventure! I couldn’t put it down for one second.<br/><br/>Outcast really defined Torak and Renn’s character. I loved how we got to know more about Renn here. To be honest, Torak and Renn aren’t really that different from each other. Even though Renn lived with her clan, she is different from her clan because of her ability to do Magecraft. I just love the parallel between Torak and Renn. Also we got to see more of Bale! I </span>
  <span id="freeText18270085842618374559" style="display:none">This series just keeps getting better and better! Outcast was a non-stop thrilling adventure! I couldn’t put it down for one second.<br /><br />Outcast really defined Torak and Renn’s character. I loved how we got to know more about Renn here. To be honest, Torak and Renn aren’t really that different from each other. Even though Renn lived with her clan, she is different from her clan because of her ability to do Magecraft. I just love the parallel between Torak and Renn. Also we got to see more of Bale! I really like him. It’s nice to him team up with Renn to help Torak. My heart goes out to Torak. He has been through so much and he’s just fourteen!<br /><br />The plot was simply fantastic! There were so many twists. The biggest and most unexpected surprise has got to be Renn’s. I didn’t see that coming at all. Not at all. My jaw dropped when I found out. There were so many events that happened caught me by surprise. I treasured this feeling okay? When Torak revealed his tattoo though. That scene gave me the chills. It was dreadful. And when Torak found out about Renn’s secret. I was kinda angry with his reaction to be honest. Dude, you had your secret and this is Renn for gods sake! She’s your best-friend! She saved your life countless times. Just give her a chance to explain will you. But in the end, everything was settled nicely so that made me extremely happy.<br /><br />Wow, I cannot believe that four books have gone by. Only two books left in this amazing series. I am not ready to say goodbye. I don’t think I’ll ever be. Sobs. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18270085842618374559" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48483884-michael-finocchiaro?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>,

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2041146481" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer18192618253599658006">Yes! Michelle Paver does it again with this splendid entry in her Chronicles of Ancient Darkness series. Torak is alone and soul sick and we wonder whether Seshru, the Soul Eater and Viper Mage will get the fire opal and conquer him or whether Bale and Renn will save him in time. And Wolf...<br/>As always, we are spellbound with the vivid evocation of this world long ago and the wonder of discovery and friendship of the characters. There are painful revelations here as we pass the summit of the story</span>
  <span id="freeText18192618253599658006" style="display:none">Yes! Michelle Paver does it again with this splendid entry in her Chronicles of Ancient Darkness series. Torak is alone and soul sick and we wonder whether Seshru, the Soul Eater and Viper Mage will get the fire opal and conquer him or whether Bale and Renn will save him in time. And Wolf...<br />As always, we are spellbound with the vivid evocation of this world long ago and the wonder of discovery and friendship of the characters. There are painful revelations here as we pass the summit of the story and head towards the last two books - certainly the confrontations with the remaining soul eaters will be paramount. In the meantime, I derive an incredible amount of satisfaction from this series reading it with my son and rooting for Torak, Renn and Wolf!</span>

  <span id="freeText13769595167518453924" style="display:none">Tyler, 8yrs, said it was very dramatic and very good. He really likes this series.<br /><br />Update 3/17/13 - my review:<br />Now I know what Tyler meant by dramatic. This book tore my heart out. It was so hard to watch Torak go through so many painful experiences - becoming an outcast and watching him suffer from soul-sickness. He begins to make choices that are against the laws of the Forest and clans. I found myself shocked and fearing for him. The pain that wolf feels as he is rebuffed by Torak and finding himself caught between two clans. Then as if there couldn't be more...finding out the secret that Renn has been carrying all this time.<br /><br />This by far has been the darkest book in the series. I did not realize just how invested I was in these characters until we all had to go on this painful journey together. And while Soul Eater was also quite dark - there was a sense of many against the evil. I felt more hopeful. Being an outcast in this book.. Torak being completely alone; it felt so very hopeless.<br /><br />This remains Tyler and I's favorite series. Onto the Oath Breaker....</span>

    <a title="Jennie Louwes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/89985522-jennie-louwes"><img alt="Jennie Louwes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584340118p2/89985522.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2778584840?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennie Louwes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennie Louwes" href="/user/show/89985522-jennie-louwes">Jennie Louwes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2778584840" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7246992526591074644">From start to finish a 5 star rating through and through. What a ride! Whew! <br/><br/>When the books in this series were first emerging I was a newlywed, charting three new courses at once: Wifedom, Motherhood, and the Wilds of Alaska. Overly preoccupied at the time I somehow managed to not see (or hear) of these books.<br/><br/>Late to the party but shouting from the rooftops now! "The Chronicles of Ancient Darkness, a book series not to be missed!"<br/><br/>"Outcast", more than any of the other books (thus far) surprised </span>
  <span id="freeText7246992526591074644" style="display:none">From start to finish a 5 star rating through and through. What a ride! Whew! <br /><br />When the books in this series were first emerging I was a newlywed, charting three new courses at once: Wifedom, Motherhood, and the Wilds of Alaska. Overly preoccupied at the time I somehow managed to not see (or hear) of these books.<br /><br />Late to the party but shouting from the rooftops now! "The Chronicles of Ancient Darkness, a book series not to be missed!"<br /><br />"Outcast", more than any of the other books (thus far) surprised me the most! The twists? The turns? The truths uncovered? I didn't see them coming! <br /><br />Not being able to see the big surprises in advance, (so wrapped up was I in the unfolding story), the entire read (layer upon layer) was captivating, disturbing, heart-wrenching, and ultimately refreshing. <br /><br />To me, this 4th installment had the best (most heartfelt and heartening) story ending to date. Finally, after closing the back cover, I feel as though I'm free to breathe deeply again; and, for a moment, all is well within the world.<br /><br />Michelle Paver, what a talent! Her words provide such rich detail, (never dull or overindulgent), just the right amount to sink you deeper within the story being read. Truly, a tremendous, gifted, authoress!<br /><br />Up next, on deck? The "Oath Breaker". A good night's rest then, the journey towards darkness continues; it all must be vanquished. No stone left unturned.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7246992526591074644" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/35835354" />
    <a title="Liisa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1084654-liisa"><img alt="Liisa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1482234979p2/1084654.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/35835354?book_show_action=true">Oct 21, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liisa" href="/user/show/1084654-liisa">Liisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Liisa by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/1869453-lyndsay">Lyndsay</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1084654-liisa?shelf=vampire-werewolves-witches-mystical">vampire-werewolves-witches-mystical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1084654-liisa?shelf=trilogies-and-series">trilogies-and-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1084654-liisa?shelf=from-the-library">from-the-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1084654-liisa?shelf=all-time-favourite-authors">all-time-favourite-authors</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer35835354" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1731796925928779403">I have found with series, the further you delve, the sooner you'll find a book that disappoints. Not so with the Chronicles of Ancient Darkness. <b>"Outcast"</b> is the fourth in the series and as captivating, well-written and engaging as the three previous books.<br/><br/><i>Michelle Paver</i>'s series was written for children but appeals to people of all ages. (I have been hooked since the first word in <i>"Wolf Brother"</i>!)<br/><br/>Whilst completely engaged in the story, heart-pounding as the circumstances Torak, Renn and Wolf of</span>
  <span id="freeText1731796925928779403" style="display:none">I have found with series, the further you delve, the sooner you'll find a book that disappoints. Not so with the Chronicles of Ancient Darkness. <b>"Outcast"</b> is the fourth in the series and as captivating, well-written and engaging as the three previous books.<br /><br /><i>Michelle Paver</i>'s series was written for children but appeals to people of all ages. (I have been hooked since the first word in <i>"Wolf Brother"</i>!)<br /><br />Whilst completely engaged in the story, heart-pounding as the circumstances Torak, Renn and Wolf often find themselves, appears hopeless, I can't help but think how a child's mind would process it. My guess? That it awakens their imagination and introduces them to those magical worlds you often only find in books. <br /><br />When I was a child, books like this is what sparked my love for reading and I can see this giving the same gift to a whole new generation.<br /><br />A thoroughly enjoyable series. Captivating and maturing with each book ~ I can't wait to see how it all ends.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1731796925928779403" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer12624128" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2628060337021935426">"Outcast" was much darker and more chaotic than the rest of the books in this series so far. However, the outcasting posed an interesting problem that developed into an engaging, fast-moving plot. The dark and chaotic feeling of this book turned me off only a bit, but I think it's because of that (and that alone) I give it four stars instead of five. The thing with Seshru and Renn also annoyed me a bit... it just felt cliche, but it certainly did provide an interesting twist. I felt really bad f</span>
  <span id="freeText2628060337021935426" style="display:none">"Outcast" was much darker and more chaotic than the rest of the books in this series so far. However, the outcasting posed an interesting problem that developed into an engaging, fast-moving plot. The dark and chaotic feeling of this book turned me off only a bit, but I think it's because of that (and that alone) I give it four stars instead of five. The thing with Seshru and Renn also annoyed me a bit... it just felt cliche, but it certainly did provide an interesting twist. I felt really bad for Torak throughout the entire story. <br />Perhaps "Outcast" wasn't as good as its prequels, but I still enjoyed it, and I'm eager to read the rest of the books in this series. <br /><br />(PS: I just hate saying this series' name. The only thing that really irks me about these books is the horrible series name. I've hardly seen anything worse... "Shadows of Doom" is about it.)</span>

<div id="review_569120962" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/569120962?book_show_action=true">Mar 23, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda Northrup" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda Northrup" href="/user/show/5899061-amanda-northrup">Amanda Northrup</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5899061-amanda-northrup?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer569120962" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1412607268226009724">Although I read a lot of series, I find that I lose interest after just 2 or 3 books. Often the plot becomes predictable and the writing more haphazard. Not so with Michelle Paver's Chronicles of Ancient Darkness series. <i> Outcast</i> is the fourth in the series and my favorite so far.<br/><br/>The story picks up right where <i> Soul Eater</i> left off without any annoying recap. Torak is quickly outcast from the clans because he bears the mark of the Soul Eaters. Being an outcast is worse than it sounds, by law anyo</span>
  <span id="freeText1412607268226009724" style="display:none">Although I read a lot of series, I find that I lose interest after just 2 or 3 books. Often the plot becomes predictable and the writing more haphazard. Not so with Michelle Paver's Chronicles of Ancient Darkness series. <i> Outcast</i> is the fourth in the series and my favorite so far.<br /><br />The story picks up right where <i> Soul Eater</i> left off without any annoying recap. Torak is quickly outcast from the clans because he bears the mark of the Soul Eaters. Being an outcast is worse than it sounds, by law anyone who sees Torak is now obligated to kill him. On the run, Torak is pursued by the clans, but also by a Soul Eater who is desperate to use his spirit walker power.<br /><br />I found this installment in the series to be intriguing and well-paced, with lots of Paver's incredible world building and character development. Each book reveals more and more about the clans and their belief systems. The concept of soul-sickness is especially interesting in this book. The protagonists Torak, Renn, and Wolf never become static. This book does a especially wonderful job of exploring the developments of Renn and Wolf.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1412607268226009724" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2770175652" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2770175652" />
    <a title="Thomas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/63824806-thomas"><img alt="Thomas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1484326813p2/63824806.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2770175652?book_show_action=true">Jun 30, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas" href="/user/show/63824806-thomas">Thomas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2770175652&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2770175652" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1328333478784673022">This is the fourth novel of Torak’s journey to vanquish the Soul Eaters. When I read this series previously, this was my least favourite of the six novels, partly due to its content and because it is the slowest of the chronicles. Upon this reread, however, I surprised myself by enjoying it more than I expected. <br/><br/>During the events of book 3, the Soul Eater Seshru marked Torak with the Soul Eater tattoo and he has since kept this hidden from the clans. When he is exposed by the boar clan member Ak</span>
  <span id="freeText1328333478784673022" style="display:none">This is the fourth novel of Torak’s journey to vanquish the Soul Eaters. When I read this series previously, this was my least favourite of the six novels, partly due to its content and because it is the slowest of the chronicles. Upon this reread, however, I surprised myself by enjoying it more than I expected. <br /><br />During the events of book 3, the Soul Eater Seshru marked Torak with the Soul Eater tattoo and he has since kept this hidden from the clans. When he is exposed by the boar clan member Aki, the clans have no alternative but to cast him out. Torak must then survive on his own, as he did after his father died. All is not lost for our hero; his loyal Wolf will ever remain by his side.<br /><br />Once again Paver manages to draw the reader into a rich and vivid world, which is based on our own thousands of years ago. I wish I could journey to some of the fantastic locations she went to in northern Europe to research these novels because to see these places for yourself, I think, would be spectacular.<br /><br />Among the key events in Outcast, I particularly enjoyed those which occurred at Lake Axehead leading up to the finale. There were some really quite sinister and tense scenes, which I didn’t appreciate when I read it the first time round. Also, Seshru really is one sneaky, sadistic, sly piece of work, which makes entertaining reading<br /><br />Considering Soul Eater was so good before it, I remember being concerned that Outcast wouldn’t live up to expectation, but it stands strongly in its own right. Another solid 4 stars for a satisfying read. Onto the book 5 and Torak’s confrontations with the final two Soul Eaters.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1328333478784673022" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1874100970" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1874100970" />
    <a title="Briana Vallene" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33273725-briana-vallene"><img alt="Briana Vallene" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1406052215p2/33273725.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1874100970?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Briana Vallene" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Briana Vallene" href="/user/show/33273725-briana-vallene">Briana Vallene</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1874100970" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2303125200258282023">I feel like I should be enjoying this series more than I actually am. Everyone raves about the series, but I'm always slogging through the pages, trying to figure out why I'm not more invested in the story. Exciting things are happening, but I can't get myself to care. Maybe it's because of the nonstop barrage of suffering heaped on Torak. He never gets a break, but his misfortunes don't make me sympathize with him, they just feel excessive. <br/><br/>With each book that goes by, Torak annoys me more and </span>
  <span id="freeText2303125200258282023" style="display:none">I feel like I should be enjoying this series more than I actually am. Everyone raves about the series, but I'm always slogging through the pages, trying to figure out why I'm not more invested in the story. Exciting things are happening, but I can't get myself to care. Maybe it's because of the nonstop barrage of suffering heaped on Torak. He never gets a break, but his misfortunes don't make me sympathize with him, they just feel excessive. <br /><br />With each book that goes by, Torak annoys me more and more, and it's hard to pin down why exactly. Maybe he bothers me because he's another "chosen one" on his "hero's journey". Maybe it's because he's such a loner. Maybe it's the way he treats Renn, my favorite character in the series. I hate how he keeps pushing her away when she's trying to help him. The whole "trying to keep her safe" thing just irks me. Renn has proved time and time again that she is brave, smart, loyal, and competent. Honestly, I wish Renn was our protagonist instead. I'm always far more interested in what she is up to. She's main reason I'm sticking with the series. Really hoping Renn and Torak don't get together in the end, but it seems like that's where the series is heading.<br /><br />There are things I like about this series, namely the depictions of a time long long ago. I'm fascinated by the in-depth descriptions of animals, different tribes, hunting and gathering. Michelle Paver has definitely done her research. I also love the way she weaves magic into her stories, seamlessly and naturally. The suspense is also well-handled, and I want to read on to discover more about the Soul-Eaters and their secrets.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2303125200258282023" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15011924552409336894"><b>So here is the summary:</b><br/><br/>The characters in the story were the wolf pack themselves, Torak, Renn, and Wolf. The wolves had black hair cut to shoulder legnth, a fringe, tusks at their necks, and a stiff mantle. The other pack, The Willows had strips sewn in spirals in jenkins, black leaved tatoos, and a permanent frown.   <span id="freeText15011924552409336894" style="display:none"><b>So here is the summary:</b><br /><br />The characters in the story were the wolf pack themselves, Torak, Renn, and Wolf. The wolves had black hair cut to shoulder legnth, a fringe, tusks at their necks, and a stiff mantle. The other pack, The Willows had strips sewn in spirals in jenkins, black leaved tatoos, and a permanent frown. During to story, in the forest, there was Torak, who was separated from his best friend, Renn. They were both separated through the the agonizing journey of finding each other, and their group of wolves. The wolves were enemies against each wolf pack yet they found their way. Near the end, they are reunited and the 2 other wolfpacks are once again happy. <br /><br /><br />Overall, I'd give this book 5 stars because of the amount of adventures (which I like). I'd reccomend it to everyone who likes adventure (with a little touch of emotion).</span>

  <span id="freeText12580238956682864996" style="display:none">I think this was the most emotional book of the series so far. I might have shed a tear a few times.<br />The story's still as captivating and doesn't let down. Everything falls into place, and it's one of those series where you feel like the author knew where it was going from the beginning and you wonder how they knew to leave these little details that would come in handy later. <br />It's full of plot twists too! Renn's secret? I think that was the most shocking twist so far.<br />Renn's character keeps being more defined and gaining depth, and she's become one of my favourite book heroines. She's so tough! Bale is back too and it's so nice to see him again.<br />Torak's character definitely gains more depth too. He goes through so much! His relationship with Wolf is tested as well and I might have shed a few tears. His relationship with Fin-Kedinn steps us and it's one of the highlights of the book! <br />4 books into this series and it hasn't let me down once, I can't believe there's only 2 books left. :(</span>

<div id="review_792962077" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/792962077" />
    <a title="Lala" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5782406-lala"><img alt="Lala" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1535544882p2/5782406.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/792962077?book_show_action=true">Dec 17, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lala" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lala" href="/user/show/5782406-lala">Lala</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5782406-lala?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5782406-lala?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5782406-lala?shelf=fav-authours">fav-authours</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer792962077" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11314555294944359309">"I am your pack, Torak said."<br/><br/>Paver does it again. These books are really quite incredible and I absolutely love them. I cannot wait to read the last two in the series. I have been taking my time with these and they are just so enjoyable. Torak, Wolf, Renn and Bale make up this adventure…and an adventure it is! The growing relationship between Torak and Renn is starting to make me nuts haha…but I'm loving it, I'm hopeful Paver will continue to develop these two. This time we find Torak being Outc</span>
  <span id="freeText11314555294944359309" style="display:none">"I am your pack, Torak said."<br /><br />Paver does it again. These books are really quite incredible and I absolutely love them. I cannot wait to read the last two in the series. I have been taking my time with these and they are just so enjoyable. Torak, Wolf, Renn and Bale make up this adventure…and an adventure it is! The growing relationship between Torak and Renn is starting to make me nuts haha…but I'm loving it, I'm hopeful Paver will continue to develop these two. This time we find Torak being Outcast…and I was pretty upset with the way this story started off, but soon Torak and Wolf were on their own in that lively forest they call home and I was lost in the story. I particularly enjoyed seeing Bale return to the series and befriend Renn and the ending was one of my favourites. Looking forward to Oath Breaker next. And once again…hvala Matic &lt;3 <br /><br />"Because that's how it is. Everything changes, all the time. Mostly, you don't notice."<br /><br />"Wolf gave a startled yelp- Torak burst into the sunshine in a glitter of droplets - and they wrestled. Wolf play growling, Torak shouting with laughter. He was happy. He could live like this for ever."<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_1448188618" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1448188618" />
    <a title="Big Pete" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47746222-big-pete"><img alt="Big Pete" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1469016966p2/47746222.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1448188618?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Big Pete" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Big Pete" href="/user/show/47746222-big-pete">Big Pete</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1448188618" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer298568266085283967"><i>Outcast</i> follows <i>Soul Eater</i>, and is as dark as its predecessor. <br/>Picking up two months later, Torak's Soul-Eater tattoo is discovered during a brawl, and he is outcast by the clans, his only allies Renn and his Seal-Clan cousin Bale. <br/>Out of all the novels, it's the most painful to read. Both Torak and Renn go through the meat-grinder in this one, physically and psychologically. <br/>I preferred <i>Soul Eater</i> to this one, probably because <i>Outcast</i> is so tragic a read. Alone, without Wolf, and becoming sicke</span>
  <span id="freeText298568266085283967" style="display:none"><i>Outcast</i> follows <i>Soul Eater</i>, and is as dark as its predecessor. <br />Picking up two months later, Torak's Soul-Eater tattoo is discovered during a brawl, and he is outcast by the clans, his only allies Renn and his Seal-Clan cousin Bale. <br />Out of all the novels, it's the most painful to read. Both Torak and Renn go through the meat-grinder in this one, physically and psychologically. <br />I preferred <i>Soul Eater</i> to this one, probably because <i>Outcast</i> is so tragic a read. Alone, without Wolf, and becoming sicker by the hour, Torak falls foul of the machinations of Seshru the Viper Mage. <i>Outcast</i> is very surreal and chaotic, but with a tight, engaging, fast-paced plot that grabs you by the throat and won't let go. <br />Michelle Paver must be congratulated on her character development - neither Torak, Renn, Fin-Kedinn or Wolf ever become static over the course of the six novels, nor have the plots become formulaic. Book by book, more is revealed about the culture, survival skills and beliefs of the clans, and that world is fascinating. <br />Not the very best of the series, but a strong, tragic and well-written entry nonetheless.</span>
  <a data-text-id="298568266085283967" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer128927147" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5337589662135810621">This is the fourth book in the Chronicles of Ancient Darkness series and, although its premise is much darker and heart-wrenching than the previous three, I still found it to be exceptionally well-written and engaging. Torak is outcast and falls prey to the soul sickness. He is mercilessly hunted by the other clans and forced to elude them while at the same time trying to find the Soul Eaters. Ms. Paver's descriptions of his struggles to survive are so vivid and stark, you can feel his pain and </span>
  <span id="freeText5337589662135810621" style="display:none">This is the fourth book in the Chronicles of Ancient Darkness series and, although its premise is much darker and heart-wrenching than the previous three, I still found it to be exceptionally well-written and engaging. Torak is outcast and falls prey to the soul sickness. He is mercilessly hunted by the other clans and forced to elude them while at the same time trying to find the Soul Eaters. Ms. Paver's descriptions of his struggles to survive are so vivid and stark, you can feel his pain and despair as though it were your own. The story also depicts the extraordinary power of friendship and love. If you enjoyed the first three books in this series, you'll be sure to enjoy this one as well.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5337589662135810621" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2255574831" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2255574831" />
    <a title="Emma Larsson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52012594-emma-larsson"><img alt="Emma Larsson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1455064267p2/52012594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2255574831?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Larsson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Larsson" href="/user/show/52012594-emma-larsson">Emma Larsson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9789152300657" href="/book/show/15729596-jagad-av-klanerna">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52012594-emma-larsson?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52012594-emma-larsson?shelf=read-in-swedish">read-in-swedish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52012594-emma-larsson?shelf=three-stars">three-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52012594-emma-larsson?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2255574831&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2255574831" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1220820560186081150">This one was harder for me to listen to. It felt like it took forever to get somewhere, and then it all happened very quickly in the end. The reunion, the flood, the murder and boom it was the end. The journey there took forever though.<br/><br/><b>But now I'll not be too negative, because that's no fun. Let's talk about what I DID like first:</b><br/><br/>- The crows. I loved the way they entered Torak's life and the bond they shared. It made me think of the Nordic god Oden and his two crows Hugin and Munin (even though </span>
  <span id="freeText1220820560186081150" style="display:none">This one was harder for me to listen to. It felt like it took forever to get somewhere, and then it all happened very quickly in the end. The reunion, the flood, the murder and boom it was the end. The journey there took forever though.<br /><br /><b>But now I'll not be too negative, because that's no fun. Let's talk about what I DID like first:</b><br /><br />- The crows. I loved the way they entered Torak's life and the bond they shared. It made me think of the Nordic god Oden and his two crows Hugin and Munin (even though Torak is noway near as cool as Oden of course).<br /><br />- The sudden twist about Seshru being Renn's mother. I was working while listening to the audiobook and when I heard that plot twist I suddenly stopped moving for a minute. If anyone had seen me they'd be thinking I suddenly got a heart attack.<br /><br />- The second time I "heart attack-stopped" in the middle of something was in the end when Fin-Kedinn announced that he's now Torak's father. It made me so warm and happy!<br /><br />- Bale. Amazing character. Not taking too much attention from the story or the other characters, while still being interesting and important.<br /><br />- Renn have had her period. Fucking finally. I don't know why but it just made me happy to read about.<br /><br />- The way Seshru wasn't Voldermort. Let me explain: The way people talk about the Soul Eaters it's like they're some sort of all powered überhuman who can never die and are as dangerous as the plague. So when I read about Torak and Renn having conversations with her just like with any other person or when I read about her doing something humanly wrong, it makes me so happy. She's just a human, a strong, evil, powerhungry human. But she's no living poison, or a ticking bomb. They can be in her presence and talk to her without risking immediate death, and I like that. It makes the villain more deep, and less, well, Voldermort'y.<br /><br />- Wolf being together with other wolves. Heartwarming to read about. However...<br /><br /><b>Things I did NOT like as much:</b><br /><br />- ... The constant "textbook" feeling it got while describing certain things, like how wolves spoke and act around each other, got old. I get that Michelle did some great research while doing these books and her entusiasm can be seen in the text, but this book had a little bit too much at times. I don't necessary know if it would've been better to erase it, maybe rewriting it. In any case, it suddenly struck me as a bit odd in the middle of the book, and I haven't had that feeling with any of the other books.<br /><br />- I somehow get the feeling, with the way he's described during the end of the book, that Fin-Kedinn will get hurt or die in the next book. I can't shake off that feeling and it annoys me, he's one of my favourite characters... That's not necessary a bad point in THIS book, but in a way it is, because it made me worry, aah!<br /><br />- And, as I said, it felt like a rollercoaster with one big leap. It was going up and up and up, then suddenly dropping in the end very quickly. I didn't expect her to die so soon, and that easily. I didn't expect it to just go *poof* "she's dead hurray and Torak's free hurray".<br /><br />- STILL no romance between these two?? Not even a mention? I'd actually be happy if it turns out they never get together in a romantic way at all and just stay as friends, but if the next book (or god forbid, the last one) suddenly drops the "oh I love him/her" bomb I'm going to be so pissed.<br /><br />All in all, the book was good, great even. It never made me frown or cuss, and was very intriguing from start to end. I can't wait to listen to the next one!</span>

<div id="review_2085814087" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2085814087" />
    <a title="Brittney Tyler" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56506626-brittney-tyler"><img alt="Brittney Tyler" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2085814087?book_show_action=true">Dec 04, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brittney Tyler" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brittney Tyler" href="/user/show/56506626-brittney-tyler">Brittney Tyler</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780060728342" href="/book/show/2179020.Outcast">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone looking for a fun read!!!!</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56506626-brittney-tyler?shelf=personal-library">personal-library</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2085814087" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7407795773714786882">Star Rating: 3.5 stars<br/><br/>Note: This is the 4th book in the Chronicles of Ancient Darkness series so this will not be an in-depth review. <br/><br/>In an effort to read all of my personally owned books in order to make Goodreads an active representation of my reading, I recently finished Outcast by Michelle Paver and I have to say that although it was a quick and exciting read, I did not enjoy it near as much as I have enjoyed some of the others in the Chronicles of Ancient Darkness series. This book is set 6</span>
  <span id="freeText7407795773714786882" style="display:none">Star Rating: 3.5 stars<br /><br />Note: This is the 4th book in the Chronicles of Ancient Darkness series so this will not be an in-depth review. <br /><br />In an effort to read all of my personally owned books in order to make Goodreads an active representation of my reading, I recently finished Outcast by Michelle Paver and I have to say that although it was a quick and exciting read, I did not enjoy it near as much as I have enjoyed some of the others in the Chronicles of Ancient Darkness series. This book is set 6,000 years ago and tells the coming-of-age story of Torak; a young Native boy who is struggling to survive on his own in a world torn apart by an unknown menace, and Torak is the only one with the powers to stop it. <br /><br />The best part about this book is the glimpse we get of the world 6,000 years ago. In each consecutive book, we get to see a different area of this world and the people that live in it- book 1 was the Forest, book 2 was the Sea, book 3 was the Far North, and book 4 was the Lake, and I believe that book 5 is the Deep Forest and book 6 is the Mountains (I am not for sure because I haven’t read those volumes yet.). As a history lover, especially an ancient history lover, I really enjoy learning about these peoples and the world that they lived in. I think it is really cool that Paver is bringing this knowledge to middle graders (This is a middle-grade series☺.) as it brings what they learn in history class to light in a way that no teacher can. I wish that this series and others like it had existed when I was actually in the age bracket for them, although I believe that there shouldn’t be an age bracket on reading at all, especially since everyone reads at a different speed and level and they shouldn’t be ashamed of that. <br /><br />Although I do enjoy these books and the knowledge that they let kids access, I didn’t enjoy this book as much as some of the others. Throughout this series, we learn about a conspiracy to usurp the power of the World Spirit being perpetuated by a group of Mages/clan shamans called the Soul Eaters. We also learn that Torak is connected to the Soul Eaters and that because of the circumstances of his birth; he is the only one who can stop them. Throughout the entire series, characters have been alluding to events that happened at or around the time of Torak’s birth, but those events are never explained, although it is obvious that they are very important to the overarching plot. Also, towards the end of the book, there were jumps in the plot like things had been omitted that shouldn’t have been. For instance, at one point, the main characters are talking on the beach and the next, Torak is in a boat trying to warn the clans at the clan meet of an impending flood. There was no smooth transition and the jump was incredibly jarring and noticeable. It is because of the plot holes and jarring transitions that I have to rate this book only 3.5 stars. <br /><br />All in all, this book was enjoyable, although the plot was not as concise and as tight as I wanted it to be. It is worth the read if you are interested to learn how people survived 6,000 years ago. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7407795773714786882" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781842551158" href="/book/show/3222762-outcast">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2844611807" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3245781501718727086"><b>
  <i>Chronicles of Ancient Darkness: Outcast</i>
</b> is the fourth book in the series and probably one of the better ones that I have read so far.<br/><br/>In this book, as the title suggests, Torak is outcast from the clans; after he is accused of taking something from the Boar Clan chief's son and then fighting with him and his clansmen (and women), only to reveal the Soul Eater tattoo taht he sports on his chest. <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[We also find out that Torak's mother actually dubbed him as clanless, when there is </span></span>
  <span id="freeText3245781501718727086" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>Chronicles of Ancient Darkness: Outcast</i>
</b> is the fourth book in the series and probably one of the better ones that I have read so far.<br /><br />In this book, as the title suggests, Torak is outcast from the clans; after he is accused of taking something from the Boar Clan chief's son and then fighting with him and his clansmen (and women), only to reveal the Soul Eater tattoo taht he sports on his chest. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[We also find out that Torak's mother actually dubbed him as clanless, when there is a surprise visit from the elusive Wolf Clan. I always assumed that since Torak could communicate with wolves that he must be Wolf Clan, but apparently that doesn't cut it. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> In his outcast state, Torak must now be on the run from the clans, as anyone who finds him has to kill him - even his supporters; Renn, Finn-Kedinn and Bale. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Of course, this does not happen, as Renn and Bale constantly try to help Torak, but their assistance is shunned as the outcast begins feeling the soul sickness that is apparently brought on by the Soul Eater from the Snake Clan. It is during this time that the clans all attempt to hunt down Torak, as they believe that he is the Soul Eater spreading sickness across the lake and its surrounds.<br /><br />Eventually, Torak - with Renn's magical help - fights through the sickness and comes face-to-face with Seshru (the Snake Clan Soul Eater). He figures out her plans to destroy the clans by flooding the area around the lake and tries to get Renn and Bale to help warn them. Though Renn is in no mood for this after the revelation that Seshru is her mother and Bale has had his skinboat destroyed. However, the clans are saved by Torak and he is eventually allowed to return, as Finn-Kedinn adopts Torak into the Raven Clan. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I still get annoyed by the state of Torak and Renn's relationship, as it really makes no sense. The author, Michelle Paver, seems to drift from Torak and Renn having a close relationship to them having a relationship in which they don't trust each other. I don't understand why, after three earlier books, where this sort of by-play was happening - Torak not telling Renn certain secrets and Renn not telling Torak certain secrets, only to have them both get upset with each other when the secrets are revealed. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[In this book, Torak keeps the Soul Eater tattoo that was forced upon him a secret, until he is found out, and Renn still helps him out, even though she is upset about not being told. Meanwhile, Renn keeps the fact that her mother is Seshru the Soul Eater a secret and Torak totally loses it, as though his secret was not as big a deal as hers. I just didn't like that it was all happening again. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Each book has had this sort of thing and it's just getting annoying now, so I hope that they are at a place where they trust each other now.<br /><br />Overall a much better book than its predecessors.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3245781501718727086" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9788202275716" href="/book/show/25749474-utst-tt">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2001508653" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13843340700080654228">I had forgotten how much I liked these books!<br/>Maybe it had something to do with the fact that I haven't been able to read in a while, or the feelings this book takes up - but I don't like them! I LOVE them! <br/>I lost count of how many times I started crying, because even though it's a completely different time people still experience the same feelings and some of the same fears. <br/>The series is set to the Stone Age, and the humans live WITH nature and paint a very good picture of what that is about. T</span>
  <span id="freeText13843340700080654228" style="display:none">I had forgotten how much I liked these books!<br />Maybe it had something to do with the fact that I haven't been able to read in a while, or the feelings this book takes up - but I don't like them! I LOVE them! <br />I lost count of how many times I started crying, because even though it's a completely different time people still experience the same feelings and some of the same fears. <br />The series is set to the Stone Age, and the humans live WITH nature and paint a very good picture of what that is about. They live in clans, and believe in something beyond being human - offering some of their food to their clan-creature for protection. Or to the forest. Releasing the spirits of the animals they hunt for food - and using as much as the animal as possible - not letting anything go to waste. <br />Torak being excellent at reading the forest and find tracks. <br />His best friend is also a wolf, his Packbrother, and he himself is sometimes more like a wolf than a human - being able to communicate with this animal. <br />The author does an excellent job with describing the life, surroundings, relationships and the spirituality of both the humans and the animals. Based on knowledge and observations - she know what she writes about by heart as well. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13843340700080654228" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked

    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {

    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

Better tomorrow than today.&quot; Harder work means the citizens of Aramanth can keep moving forward to improved life stations--from Gray tenements and Orange apartments, upwards to glorious mansions of White. Only some families, like the Haths, believe more in ideas and dreams than in endless toil and ratings. When Kestrel Hath decides she is through with the Aramanth work ethic, she is joined in her small rebellion by her twin brother Bowman and their friend Mumpo. Together, they set the orderly city on its ear by escaping Aramanth\'s walls for an adventure that takes them from city sewers to desert sandstorms. Guided by an archaic map, they know that if they can find the voice of the Wind Singer, an ancient and mysterious instrument that stands in the center of Aramanth, they can save their people from their dreamless existence. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer7595484941866695400">Michelle Paver was born in Central Africa, but came to England as a child. After gaining a degree in Biochemistry from Oxford University, she became a partner in a City law firm, but eventually gave that up to write full-time.<br/><br/>The hugely successful <i>Chronicles of Ancient Darkness</i> series arose from Michelle's lifelong passion for animals, anthropology and the distant past - as as well as an encounter</span>
  <span id="freeText7595484941866695400" style="display:none">Michelle Paver was born in Central Africa, but came to England as a child. After gaining a degree in Biochemistry from Oxford University, she became a partner in a City law firm, but eventually gave that up to write full-time.<br /><br />The hugely successful <i>Chronicles of Ancient Darkness</i> series arose from Michelle's lifelong passion for animals, anthropology and the distant past - as as well as an encounter with a large bear in a remote valley in southern California. To research the books, Michelle has traveled to Finland, Greenland, Sweden, Norway, Arctic Canada and the Carpathian Mountains. She has slept on reindeer skins, swum with wild orca (killer whales), and got nose-to-nose with polar bears - and, of course, wolves. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7595484941866695400" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
